Alternative Interpretation of Tasdiq and Objection-Answer
Author presents an alternative interpretation of the division of knowledge and responds to an objection based on the author's definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the debate between the alternative interpretation and the author's definition of tasdiq and evaluate the objections.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is not simply a composite; it is cognition subject to judgment.

This passage delves into a subtle distinction in the definition of tasdiq. Some scholars propose that tasdiq is cognition that is the subject (ma'rud) of judgment, not the composite of cognition and judgment. The author then presents an objection based on the original text's definition and refutes it. Understanding this debate clarifies the precise nature of assent in Islamic logic and epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions of tasdiq
The alternative view says tasdiq is cognition subject (ma'rud) to judgment. The author's view defines tasdiq as the composite (majmu' murakkab) of cognition and judgment. Note the difference.
2
Understand the alternative interpretation
According to this view, if cognition is not subject to judgment, it is tasawwur; if it is subject, it is tasdiq. This prevents the earlier problem of generating multiple tasdiqat from a single judgment.
This is a nuanced position that avoids the critique of producing many tasdiqs.
3
Follow the objection
The objector says: 'The author (al-musannif) explicitly defined tasdiq as the composite of cognition and judgment, which is exactly the position of Imam al-Razi.' This challenges the alternative view.
4
Analyze the response
The response argues that the author's definition fails: if tasdiq is the second part of the division (cognition with judgment), it is not the composite; if it is the composite, it is a combination of two heterogeneous elements and not a part of knowledge. Thus the definition is self-defeating.
The response uses a form of logical objection (mu'arada) by showing the definition leads to absurdity.
5
Evaluate the debate
Consider which definition is more coherent and why the alternative interpretation might be preferred. The key is that the alternative avoids making tasdiq a mere composite.
This debate illustrates the importance of precise definitions in Islamic logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من قال : معنى هذا التقسيم أن الإدراك إن لم يكن معروضاً للحكم فهو القسم الأول، وإن كان معروضاً له فهو التصديق، وحينئذ لا يلزم أن يكون تصور المحكوم عليه وحده أو تصوّر المحكوم به وحده ولا مجموعهما معاً ولا أحدهما مع النسبة الحكمية تصديقا لكن يلزم أن يكون مجموع التصورات الثلاث تصديقاً - لأنه إدراك معروض للحكم - بل يلزم أن يكون إدراك النسبة وحدها تصديقاً، لأن الحكم عارض له حقيقة، ويلزم أيضاً أن يكون الحكم خارجاً عن التصديق عارضاً له. فإن قلت : قد صرّح المصنف بأن المجموع المركب من الإدراك والحكم يسمى بالتصديق، وذلك مذهب الإمام بعينه. قلت : ذلك لا يجديه نفعاً لأنّ القسم الثاني - الخارج عن التقسيم - هو الإدراك المجامع للحكم، لا المجموع المركب منهما، فإن كان التصديق عبارة عن القسم الثاني، فالحال على ما عرفت من عدم انطباقه على شيء من المذهبين وفساده في نفسه، وإن كان عبارة عن المجموع المركب منهما – كما صرح به - لم يكن التصديق قسماً من العلم، بل مركباً من أحد قسميه مع آخر مقارن له - أعني الحكم - وذلك باطل. وأيضاً يصدق على تصوّر المحكوم عليه والحكم معاً أنه مجموع مركب من إدراك وحكم، فيلزم أن يكون تصديقاً.
Some said: The meaning of this division is that if cognition is not subject to judgment, it is the first part (tasawwur), and if it is subject to judgment, it is tasdiq. Then it does not follow that the conception of the subject alone, or the conception of the predicate alone, or both together, or one of them together with the relational judgment, is a tasdiq; rather, it follows that the sum of the three conceptions is a tasdiq—because it is cognition subject to judgment—indeed, it follows that the conception of the relation alone is a tasdiq, because judgment actually inheres in it, and it also follows that the judgment is external to the tasdiq and accidental to it. If you say: The author explicitly stated that the composite of cognition and judgment is called tasdiq, and that is precisely the position of Imam al-Razi. I say: That does not help him, because the second part—which is external to the division—is the cognition that accompanies judgment, not the composite. So if tasdiq is the second part, the situation is as you know, that it does not correspond to either school and is invalid in itself; and if it is the composite of the two—as he stated—then tasdiq is not a part of knowledge, but rather a composite of one of its parts with another concomitant—namely, judgment—and that is false. Also, the combination of the conception of the subject and the judgment is true as a composite of cognition and judgment, so it would follow that it is a tasdiq.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents an alternative interpretation of the division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq. According to this view, tasdiq is simply cognition that is the subject (ma'rud) of judgment, not the composite of cognition and judgment. This is a nuanced position that avoids the earlier critique of generating multiple tasdiqat. The author then introduces an objection: the author of the original text (al-musannif) explicitly defined tasdiq as the composite. The response argues that this definition fails because it either reduces tasdiq to a part of the division (which is not the composite) or makes tasdiq a composite of two heterogeneous elements, which would mean it is not a genuine part of knowledge. Furthermore, any combination of a conception and a judgment would then qualify as a tasdiq, leading to absurdity. This exchange clarifies the distinction between the simple and composite views.

Key Terms
معروض (ma'rud): The subject or bearer of something; here, cognition is the ma'rud of judgment, meaning judgment inheres in it.
عارض ('arid): Accidental; judgment is described as 'arid (accidental) to tasdiq in one interpretation.
مجموع مركب (majmu' murakkab): Composite sum; the combination of cognition and judgment as a single unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key claim of the alternative interpretation regarding tasdiq?
A) It is the composite of cognition and judgment
B) It is cognition that is subject to judgment
C) It is identical to judgment
D) It is the sum of all conceptions

Key Takeaway
The alternative interpretation defines tasdiq as cognition subject to judgment, avoiding the problems inherent in defining it as a composite.

Three Differences on Tasdiq: Philosophers vs. Imam al-Razi
Author enumerates three points of disagreement on tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the philosophers' and Imam al-Razi's positions on the simplicity of tasdiq, the role of conception, and the nature of judgment.

Core Idea
The nature of tasdiq is debated: is it simple or composite?

In this lesson, we examine three critical points of disagreement between the philosophers (followers of Avicenna) and Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi regarding the nature of tasdiq (assent). These differences are not mere technicalities; they have implications for how we understand the structure of knowledge and the relationship between conception and judgment. The passage presents a concise list, intended for memorization as a foundation for deeper study.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the First Difference: Simplicity vs. Compositeness
Philosophers say tasdiq is simple (basit) – an indivisible act. Imam al-Razi says it is composite (murakkab), consisting of conception and judgment.
2
Memorize the Second Difference: Status of Conception
For philosophers, conception of subject, predicate, and relation is an external condition (shart kharij) for tasdiq. For al-Razi, it is an internal part (shatr dakhil) of tasdiq.
3
Memorize the Third Difference: Judgment as Identity or Part
Philosophers identify judgment (hukm) with tasdiq itself. Al-Razi says judgment is only a part of tasdiq.
4
Contrast the Two Positions
Notice how al-Razi's composite view consistently makes both conception and judgment internal components, while philosophers treat them as external or identical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحدها أنّ التصديق بسيط على مذهب الحكماء، ومركب على رأي الإمام. وثانيها : أن تصوّر الطرفين والنسبة شرط للتصديق خارج قولهم، وشطره الداخل فيه على قوله. وثالثها : أن الحكم نفس التصديق على زعمهم، وجزؤه الداخل على زعمه.

Third: Judgment is identical to tasdiq according to them, and a part of its interior according to him.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This is a straightforward enumeration of three key doctrinal differences between the philosophers (al-hukama', likely Avicenna and his followers) and Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi concerning tasdiq. The first point: for philosophers, tasdiq is a simple act of assent; for al-Razi, it is a composite of conception and judgment. The second: for philosophers, the conceptions of subject, predicate, and relation are external conditions (shart) for tasdiq; for al-Razi, they are internal components (shatr damin). The third: for philosophers, judgment itself is identical to tasdiq; for al-Razi, judgment is only a part of tasdiq. This concise summary is essential for students to memorize as it encapsulates the core debate in Islamic logic about the structure of assent.

Two Objections to the Standard Division of Knowledge
Author explains why he altered the famous division of knowledge and gives two objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the two logical objections to the famous division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq.

Core Idea
The famous division of knowledge leads to logical contradictions: a part cannot be a counterpart, and a single proposition generates multiple absurd assents.

In this passage, the author of the matn explains why he deviated from the well-known division of knowledge into conception (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq). He presents two objections that reveal inherent logical flaws in the standard classification. Understanding these objections is crucial for correctly applying the epistemic categories in logic and Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the standard division being critiqued
The text begins by stating the famous division: 'knowledge is either conception or assent'. Locate this in the Arabic and note the terms.
2
Understand the first objection: part/counterpart contradiction
The author argues that the division forces either a part (qism) to be a counterpart (qasim) of the whole, or a counterpart to be a part, both of which are impossible. This is a logical flaw in the classification scheme.
In logical classification, a part (species) cannot be a counterpart (coordinate division) of the whole (genus), and vice versa.
3
Understand the second objection: multiplication of assents
The author shows that analyzing a proposition like 'Zayd is writing' into its components (conception of predicate, relational judgment, etc.) would generate multiple distinct tasdiqat, up to seven, which is absurd. This demonstrates the division leads to an infinite regress.
4
Recognize the author's solution
To avoid these problems, the author replaces 'tasawwur' with 'pure conception' (al-tasawwur al-sadhij) and reinterprets 'tasdiq' as 'assenting conception' (al-tasawwur al-musaddiq), thereby sidestepping the logical contradictions.
This redefinition prevents the part/counterpart issue and the multiplication of assents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنّ المشهور فيها بين القوم أنّ العلم إما تصوّر وإما تصديق» والمصنف عدل عنه إلى التصور الساذج وإلى التصديق، وسبب العدول ورود الاعتراض على التقسيم المشهور من وجهين : الأول أن التقسيم فاسد، لأن أحد الأمرين لازم : وهو إما أن يكون قسم الشيء قسيماً له ، أو يكون قسيم الشيء قسماً منه؛ وهما باطلان. وكذا يكون تصوّر المحكوم به مع الحكم تصديقاً آخر، وهكذا تصوّر النسبة الحكمية مع الحكم تصديقاً ثالثاً، وكذا المجموع المركب من هذه التصورات الثلاثة والحكم تصديقاً رابعاً، ويحصل من تركيب اثنين منها مع الحكم ثلاثة أخرى، فيرتقي عدد التصديقات إلى سبعة أيضاً، إلا أن أحد هذه السبعة هو مذهب الإمام بخلاف السبعة السابقة (شريف).
Know that the well-known division among the people is that knowledge is either conception or assent, and the author deviated from it to pure conception and to assenting conception. The reason for the deviation is that an objection was raised against the well-known division from two aspects: First, the division is invalid because one of two things is necessary: either a part of a thing is a counterpart of it, or a counterpart of a thing is a part of it; and both are false. Likewise, the conception of the predicate together with the judgment would be another tasdiq, and similarly the conception of the relational judgment together with the judgment would be a third tasdiq, and similarly the composite of these three conceptions plus the judgment would be a fourth tasdiq, and from combining two of them with the judgment three more arise, so the number of tasdiqat rises to seven again, except that one of these seven is the position of Imam al-Razi in contrast to the previous seven.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage explains why the author of the original text (al-musannif) modified the standard division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq. The standard division, when analyzed, leads to a logical contradiction: a part (qism) of a thing cannot be its counterpart (qasim), and vice versa. The author gives a detailed example showing that if we take a proposition like 'Zayd is writing' and try to treat various components as independent tasdiqat, we again end up with seven tasdiqat, one of which matches Imam al-Razi's view. This demonstrates the confusion inherent in the famous division. The author's decision to use 'pure conception' (al-tasawwur al-sadhij) and 'assenting conception' (al-tasawwur al-musaddiq) is intended to avoid these paradoxes. The two objections are: (1) the logical impossibility of a part being a counterpart and vice versa, and (2) the generation of multiple tasdiqat from a single proposition, which is absurd.

8 min
The Part-Counterpart Problem in Knowledge Division
Author presents the first objection to the famous division of knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical error of confusing a part with a counterpart in any taxonomic division, using the example of tasawwur and tasdiq.

Core Idea
A valid division must keep parts and counterparts distinct; confusing them destroys the division.

The famous division of knowledge into conception and assent seems straightforward, but the first objection reveals a fatal flaw: if tasdiq is defined as perception-plus-judgment, it becomes a part of conception, yet in the division it is treated as a counterpart. This lesson unpacks that logical misstep.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish part (qism) from counterpart (qasim)
A part (qism) is subsumed under the divided whole and is more specific (e.g., 'rational animal' is a part of 'animal'). A counterpart (qasim) is coordinate under a higher genus ('rational animal' and 'non-rational animal' are counterparts under 'animal').
This distinction is crucial for evaluating any division.
2
Identify the definitions in the famous division
In the famous division, 'knowledge' is divided into 'conception' (tasawwur) and 'assent' (tasdiq). Tasdiq is often defined as 'perception together with judgment' (al-tasawwur ma‘a al-hukm).
3
Check if tasdiq is a part or counterpart of conception
If tasdiq = conception + judgment, then conception is a component of tasdiq. Therefore, tasdiq is NOT a part of conception (it is broader), but rather conception is a part of tasdiq. Yet in the division, tasdiq is presented as a counterpart of conception.
This is the heart of the first objection.
4
Recognize the two impossible outcomes
The objection states: either a part of something is made its counterpart (if tasdiq is a part of conception but treated as counterpart) or a counterpart is made a part (if judgment is a counterpart of conception but tasdiq is treated as a part of knowledge = conception). Both are absurd.
This shows the division is corrupt unless definitions change.
5
Apply the rule to any division
As an exercise, check any other binary division in Islamic sciences (e.g., 'ibadah divided into physical and financial). Ensure that neither part is a subset of the other and that they are truly coordinate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحدها أنّ التصديق بسيط على مذهب الحكماء، ومركب على رأي الإمام. وثانيها : أن تصوّر الطرفين والنسبة شرط للتصديق خارج قولهم، وشطره الداخل فيه على قوله. وثالثها : أن الحكم نفس التصديق على زعمهم، وجزؤه الداخل على زعمه. واعلم أنّ المشهور فيها بين القوم أنّ العلم إما تصوّر وإما تصديق» والمصنف عدل عنه إلى التصور الساذج وإلى التصديق، وسبب العدول ورود الاعتراض على التقسيم المشهور من وجهين : الأول أن التقسيم فاسد، لأن أحد الأمرين لازم : وهو إما أن يكون قسم الشيء قسيماً له ، أو يكون قسيم الشيء قسماً منه؛ وهما باطلان. وكذا يكون تصوّر المحكوم به مع الحكم تصديقاً آخر، وهكذا تصوّر النسبة الحكمية مع الحكم تصديقاً ثالثاً، وكذا المجموع المركب من هذه التصورات الثلاثة والحكم تصديقاً رابعاً، ويحصل من تركيب اثنين منها مع الحكم ثلاثة أخرى، فيرتقي عدد التصديقات إلى سبعة أيضاً، إلا أن أحد هذه السبعة هو مذهب الإمام بخلاف السبعة السابقة (شريف). One of them is that tasdiq is simple according to the philosophers, and composite according to the opinion of the Imam. The second is that the conception of the two extremes and the relation is a condition for tasdiq extrinsic to their statement, and its intrinsic part according to his statement. The third is that the judgment itself is tasdiq according to their claim, and its intrinsic part according to his claim. Know that the well-known among the people is that knowledge is either conception or assent, and the author turned away from it to bare conception and to assent, and the reason for turning away is the occurrence of objection to the well-known division from two aspects: the first is that the division is corrupt because one of two things is necessary: either that a part of something is made a counterpart to it, or that a counterpart of something is made a part of it; and both are false. Likewise, the conception of the thing judged together with the judgment becomes another assent, and thus the conception of the relative judgment together with the judgment becomes a third assent, and likewise the composite sum of these three conceptions and the judgment becomes a fourth assent, and from combining two of them with the judgment three others result, so the number of assents rises to seven also, except that one of these seven is the doctrine of the Imam contrary to the previous seven (Sharif). (1) The part of a thing is that which is subsumed under it and more specific than it, and the counterpart of a thing is that which is opposite to it and subsumed with it under another thing; for example, if you divide animal into 'rational animal' and 'non-rational animal', each of them is a part of animal and a counterpart of the other. The meaning of making a part of something a counterpart to it is that that thing is a part of it in reality and you have made it a counterpart to it; and the meaning of making a counterpart of something a part of it is the opposite of that (Sharif). That is because if tasdiq is expression for conception together with judgment, and conception with judgment is a part of conception, but in the well-known division it is made a counterpart to it, then that is making a part of something a counterpart to it – that is the first matter. And if it is expression for judgment, and judgment is a counterpart of conception, but in the division it is made a part of knowledge which is itself conception, then that is making a counterpart of something a part of it – that is the second matter. This objection only applies if knowledge is divided into absolute conception and assent. (1) This is based on the fact that tasdiq is expression for perception that is combined with judgment or that receives judgment, as the apparent wording of the author of Kashf and his followers – like the author and others – indicates in the division of knowledge as we explained earlier. But if by tasdiq is meant what is the doctrine of the Imam – I mean the composite sum of the three conceptions and the judgment – then it is not apparent that tasdiq in this sense is a part of conception, because it does not necessarily follow that a composite sum of a thing and another is such that that thing applies to it so that it would be a part of it and subsumed under it – do you not see that the sum of the wall and the roof is neither a roof nor a wall. Rather, in that case one must resort to what the commentator mentioned regarding tasdiq in the sense of judgment, and it is said: tasdiq in the sense of the composite sum is a part of conception, just as it in the sense of judgment is a counterpart to it, and you have made it in the division a part of knowledge which is conception itself, so that is making a counterpart of something a part of it (Sharif). Kashf al-Asrar 'an Ghawamid al-Afkar by Afdal al-Din Namawar al-Khunji, manuscript. (2) Whoever divides knowledge into absolute conception and assent did not intend by conception a general meaning encompassing assent, but rather intended by assent the perception that the relation occurs or does not occur, and intended by conception the perception of other than that, and there is no doubt that these two divisions are opposed to each other, not
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a critical discussion of the famous division of knowledge into tasawwur (conception) and tasdiq (assent). The author (the commentator on the Shamsiyya) begins by noting three points about the nature of tasdiq: first, that it is simple according to the philosophers and composite according to the Imam (likely Fakhr al-Din al-Razi); second, that the conception of the two terms and the relation is a condition for tasdiq; third, that the judgment itself is tasdiq according to some. Then the author explains that the original author (of the matn) turned away from the well-known division to 'bare conception' and 'assent' due to two objections. The first objection is that the famous division is corrupt because it leads to either making a part of something a counterpart to it, or making a counterpart of something a part of it – both of which are impossible. The second objection is that if tasdiq is defined as conception plus judgment, then the conception of the thing judged with the judgment becomes another tasdiq, the conception of the relation with the judgment becomes a third, and the composite of the three conceptions with the judgment becomes a fourth, and combinations produce seven tasdiqs, making the division unstable. The author then clarifies the definitions of 'part' (qism) and 'counterpart' (qasim) with an example from the animal division. The commentator (Sharif) provides a rebuttal: the first objection only holds if tasdiq is defined as perception combined with judgment (as per the author of Kashf and others). However, if we adopt the Imam's definition – a composite of three conceptions and judgment – then tasdiq in that sense is not a part of conception, because the composite of two things does not necessarily fall under either component. The commentator concludes by noting that even on the Imam's view, if we consider tasdiq in the sense of judgment, the difficulty returns. The passage ends with a note that the author of Kashf defined tasdiq as the perception of a relation being or not being, and conception as perception of everything else, and these two are genuinely opposed.

How Definitions of Tasdiq Affect the Knowledge Division
Author contrasts definitions of tasdiq and their effects on the division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the standard and Imam's definitions of tasdiq and explain how each definition impacts the validity of the division into tasawwur and tasdiq.

Core Idea
The definition of tasdiq determines whether the division of knowledge is logically sound.

The second objection and the commentator's rebuttal both hinge on what we mean by 'assent'. If tasdiq is perception plus judgment, it includes conception and breaks the division. But the Imam's definition—tasdiq as a composite of three conceptions and judgment—avoids the part-counterpart problem because a composite is not necessarily a part of its components. This lesson explores these definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three definitions of tasdiq mentioned
The passage mentions: (1) tasdiq as simple (philosophers), (2) tasdiq as composite of three conceptions and judgment (Imam), and (3) tasdiq as perception combined with judgment (standard logicians). Focus on (2) and (3).
2
Apply the standard definition to the division
If tasdiq = conception + judgment, then tasdiq contains conception. In the division, conception and tasdiq are presented as coordinate, but actually tasdiq is broader. This leads to the part-counterpart problem.
3
Apply the Imam's definition to the division
If tasdiq = composite of concept of subject, concept of predicate, concept of relation, plus judgment, then tasdiq is a whole whose parts are distinct from mere conception. Does this whole become a part of conception? No, because a composite is not reducible to one of its components.
The commentator uses the example: a wall plus a roof is neither a wall nor a roof.
4
Check whether the Imam's definition resolves the first objection
Since tasdiq (composite) is not a part of conception, the first objection (part vs. counterpart) does not apply. However, a new problem arises: if we consider tasdiq in the sense of judgment, it is still a counterpart of conception, and the division may still be problematic.
The commentator notes that even the Imam's definition requires care.
5
Summarize the impact of definitions on division validity
The validity of the knowledge division depends entirely on which definition of tasdiq is adopted. The standard definition leads to absurdity; the Imam's definition rescues it but introduces subtleties.
Thus, taxonomies in Islamic logic are not fixed; they depend on precise definitions.

(۱) قسم الشيء هو ماكان مندرجاً تحته وأخص منه، وقسيم الشيء هو ماكان مقابلاً له ومندرجا معه تحت شي آخر ؛ مثلاً إذا قسمت الحيوان إلى «حيوان ناطق» و«حيوان غير ناطق» كان كل واحد منهما قسماً من الحيوان وقسيماً للآخر، ومعني كون قسم الشيء قسيماً له أن يكون ذلك الشيء قسماً منه في الواقع وقد جعلته أنت قسيماً له، ومعنى كون قسيم الشيء قسماً منه عكس ذلك (شریف). وذلك لأن التصديق إن كان عبارة عن التصور مع الحكم، والتصوّر مع الحكم قسم من التصوّر، وقد جعل في التقسيم المشهور قسيماً له، فيكون قسم الشيء قسيما له - وهو الأمر الأول. وإن كان عبارة عن الحكم، والحكم قسيم للتصور، وقد جعل في التقسيم قسماً من العلم الذي هو نفس التصور، فيكون قسيم الشيء قسماً منه – وهو الأمر الثاني. وهذا الاعتراض إنما يرد إذا قسم العلم إلى مطلق التصور والتصديق) (۱) هذا بناء على أن التصديق عبارة عن الإدراك المجامع للحكم أو المعروض للحكم، كما يدل عليه ظاهر عبارة صاحب الكشف (*) وأتباعه – كالمصنف وغيره - في تقسيم العلم كما بيناه سابقا وأما إذا أريد بالتصديق ماهو مذهب الإمام - أعني المجموع المركب من التصورات الثلاث والحكم - فلايظهر أن التصديق بهذا المعنى قسم من التصوّر، إذ لا يلزم أن يكون المجموع المركب من شيء وآخر بحيث يصدق عليه ذلك الشيء حتى يكون قسماً منه ومندرجا تحته - الاترى أن مجموع الجدار والسقف لا يكون سقفاً ولا جداراً - بل يحتاج حينئذ إلى أن يتمسك بما ذكره الشارح في التصديق بمعني الحكم فيقال : التصديق بمعنى المجموع المركب قسم للتصوّر ؛ كما أنه بمعنى الحكم قسيم له أيضاً، و قد جعلته في التقسيم قسماً من العلم الذي هو نفس التصوّر فيكون قسيم الشيء قسماً منه (شريف). كشف الأسرار عن غوامض الأفكار لأفضل الدين ناماور الخنجي مخطوط. ٢) من قسم العلم إلى مطلق التصوّر والتصديق لم يرد بالتصور معنى عاماً شاملاً للتصديق، بل أراد بالتصديق إدراك أن النسبة واقعة أوليست بواقعة وأراد بالتصور إدراك ماعدا ذلك، ولاشك أن هذين القسمين متقابلان، ليس
One of them is that tasdiq is simple according to the philosophers, and composite according to the opinion of the Imam. The second is that the conception of the two extremes and the relation is a condition for tasdiq extrinsic to their statement, and its intrinsic part according to his statement. The third is that the judgment itself is tasdiq according to their claim, and its intrinsic part according to his claim. Know that the well-known among the people is that knowledge is either conception or assent, and the author turned away from it to bare conception and to assent, and the reason for turning away is the occurrence of objection to the well-known division from two aspects: the first is that the division is corrupt because one of two things is necessary: either that a part of something is made a counterpart to it, or that a counterpart of something is made a part of it; and both are false. Likewise, the conception of the thing judged together with the judgment becomes another assent, and thus the conception of the relative judgment together with the judgment becomes a third assent, and likewise the composite sum of these three conceptions and the judgment becomes a fourth assent, and from combining two of them with the judgment three others result, so the number of assents rises to seven also, except that one of these seven is the doctrine of the Imam contrary to the previous seven (Sharif). (1) The part of a thing is that which is subsumed under it and more specific than it, and the counterpart of a thing is that which is opposite to it and subsumed with it under another thing; for example, if you divide animal into 'rational animal' and 'non-rational animal', each of them is a part of animal and a counterpart of the other. The meaning of making a part of something a counterpart to it is that that thing is a part of it in reality and you have made it a counterpart to it; and the meaning of making a counterpart of something a part of it is the opposite of that (Sharif). That is because if tasdiq is expression for conception together with judgment, and conception with judgment is a part of conception, but in the well-known division it is made a counterpart to it, then that is making a part of something a counterpart to it – that is the first matter. And if it is expression for judgment, and judgment is a counterpart of conception, but in the division it is made a part of knowledge which is itself conception, then that is making a counterpart of something a part of it – that is the second matter. This objection only applies if knowledge is divided into absolute conception and assent. (1) This is based on the fact that tasdiq is expression for perception that is combined with judgment or that receives judgment, as the apparent wording of the author of Kashf and his followers – like the author and others – indicates in the division of knowledge as we explained earlier. But if by tasdiq is meant what is the doctrine of the Imam – I mean the composite sum of the three conceptions and the judgment – then it is not apparent that tasdiq in this sense is a part of conception, because it does not necessarily follow that a composite sum of a thing and another is such that that thing applies to it so that it would be a part of it and subsumed under it – do you not see that the sum of the wall and the roof is neither a roof nor a wall. Rather, in that case one must resort to what the commentator mentioned regarding tasdiq in the sense of judgment, and it is said: tasdiq in the sense of the composite sum is a part of conception, just as it in the sense of judgment is a counterpart to it, and you have made it in the division a part of knowledge which is conception itself, so that is making a counterpart of something a part of it (Sharif). Kashf al-Asrar 'an Ghawamid al-Afkar by Afdal al-Din Namawar al-Khunji, manuscript. (2) Whoever divides knowledge into absolute conception and assent did not intend by conception a general meaning encompassing assent, but rather intended by assent the perception that the relation occurs or does not occur, and intended by conception the perception of other than that, and there is no doubt that these two divisions are opposed to each other, not
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a critical discussion of the famous division of knowledge into tasawwur (conception) and tasdiq (assent). The author (the commentator on the Shamsiyya) begins by noting three points about the nature of tasdiq: first, that it is simple according to the philosophers and composite according to the Imam (likely Fakhr al-Din al-Razi); second, that the conception of the two terms and the relation is a condition for tasdiq; third, that the judgment itself is tasdiq according to some. Then the author explains that the original author (of the matn) turned away from the well-known division to 'bare conception' and 'assent' due to two objections. The first objection is that the famous division is corrupt because it leads to either making a part of something a counterpart to it, or making a counterpart of something a part of it – both of which are impossible. The second objection is that if tasdiq is defined as conception plus judgment, then the conception of the thing judged with the judgment becomes another tasdiq, the conception of the relation with the judgment becomes a third, and the composite of the three conceptions with the judgment becomes a fourth, and combinations produce seven tasdiqs, making the division unstable. The author then clarifies the definitions of 'part' (qism) and 'counterpart' (qasim) with an example from the animal division. The commentator (Sharif) provides a rebuttal: the first objection only holds if tasdiq is defined as perception combined with judgment (as per the author of Kashf and others). However, if we adopt the Imam's definition – a composite of three conceptions and judgment – then tasdiq in that sense is not a part of conception, because the composite of two things does not necessarily fall under either component. The commentator concludes by noting that even on the Imam's view, if we consider tasdiq in the sense of judgment, the difficulty returns. The passage ends with a note that the author of Kashf defined tasdiq as the perception of a relation being or not being, and conception as perception of everything else, and these two are genuinely opposed.

تصور
قسم

According to the passage, what is the Imam's definition of tasdiq?
A) Simple perception without judgment
B) Perception combined with judgment
C) The composite sum of the two concepts, the relation, and the judgment
D) The judgment itself

Key Takeaway
The definition of tasdiq is not monolithic; adopting the Imam's composite definition resolves the first objection but introduces new considerations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In a fiqh discussion, two scholars define 'ijma' differently: one as the consensus of all mujtahids, another as the consensus of the majority. Explain how each definition leads to a different set of cases that count as ijma. Which definition creates a more stable division between ijma and ikhtilaf?
?
In kalam, the division of attributes into 'essential' and 'active' depends on the definition of 'attribute'. Show how a broad definition (all qualities) vs. a narrow one (only those not identical with essence) changes the division.

Module 9 · Lesson 18

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
advanced
8 min
The Commentator's Resolution: The Imam's Definition Salvages the Division
Commentator rebuts the first objection by invoking the Imam's definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the commentator's argument that the first objection to the knowledge division is avoided when tasdiq is defined as a composite, and explain the analogy of the wall and roof.

Core Idea
A composite (murakkab) is not necessarily a part of its components, so the Imam's definition rescues the division.

The commentator (Sharif) offers a crucial refinement: the first objection only applies if tasdiq is defined as perception plus judgment. But if we adopt the Imam's definition—tasdiq as a composite of three conceptions and judgment—then tasdiq is not a part of conception, because a whole is not reducible to one of its parts. This lesson walks through that argument.

Guided Path
1
Recall the first objection and its basis
The first objection claimed the division is corrupt because it forces a part to be a counterpart or vice versa. This rests on the standard definition: tasdiq = conception + judgment.
2
Introduce the Imam's definition
The Imam (Fakhr al-Din al-Razi) defines tasdiq as a composite of: the concept of the subject, the concept of the predicate, the concept of the relation, and the judgment affirming or denying the relation.
3
Apply the part-counterpart test to the Imam's definition
Now, is this composite (tasdiq) a part of conception? No, because conception alone is just the apprehension of a term without judgment. The composite includes more than just conception. Therefore, it is not a part of conception.
The commentator gives the analogy: a wall plus a roof is neither a wall nor a roof.
4
Conclude that the first objection does not apply
Since the Imam's tasdiq is not a part of conception, it cannot be mistakenly made a counterpart. Thus the objection falls away. However, the commentator notes that if we consider tasdiq in the sense of judgment (a component of the composite), the problem may reappear.
5
Evaluate the strength of the resolution
The resolution works only if we accept the Imam's definition. It shows that the division's validity is definition-dependent. This is a key insight into the role of precise definitions in logical taxonomy.

What is the commentator's main argument for why the Imam's definition of tasdiq avoids the first objection?
A) The Imam's definition makes tasdiq simpler than the standard definition.
B) The Imam's definition makes tasdiq identical to conception.
C) A composite (like wall and roof) is not necessarily a part of its components, so tasdiq is not a part of conception.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In a fiqh debate, the definition of 'ijma' is contested: one scholar defines it as the unanimous agreement of all scholars, another as the agreement of the majority. Use the wall-roof analogy to argue whether the majority definition (which includes some but not all) can be considered a part of the unanimous definition. Which definition is more defensible as a composite?
?
Construct a similar argument for the definition of 'qiyas' (analogy). Should qiyas be defined as 'extension of a ruling from original case to new case due to shared 'illa' or as a 'compound of four components' (asl, far', hukm, 'illa)? Show how the choice of definition affects whether qiyas is a part of 'ijtihad' or a counterpart.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
advanced
10 min
Resolving the Objection on the Division of Knowledge
Author resolves an objection on the division of knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the different meanings of tasawwur and tasdiq in classical Islamic logic and explain why the objection that tasdiq is both a part and counterpart of tasawwur is invalid.

Core Idea
The ambiguity of 'tasawwur' resolves the apparent contradiction in the division of knowledge.

This passage tackles a powerful objection against the standard division of knowledge into conception (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq). The objection claims that tasdiq ends up being both a part of tasawwur and its counterpart. The commentator al-Sharif shows that this objection only works against a specific understanding of the terms, and once the homonymy of 'tasawwur' is recognized, the problem vanishes. You will learn how careful attention to definitions prevents logical errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The passage presents two formulations: (1) If tasdiq = tasawwur + hukm, then it is a part of tasawwur but is made its counterpart. (2) If tasdiq = hukm, then hukm is a counterpart of tasawwur, but tasdiq is made a part of knowledge (identified with tasawwur).
2
Note the two meanings of tasawwur
Tasawwur can mean (a) perception without judgment (specific), or (b) absolute perception synonymous with knowledge (general). The objection confuses these meanings.
This is the key insight: the word 'tasawwur' is used homonymously.
3
See how the resolution works
If by tasawwur we mean the specific sense, then tasdiq (as perception of a relation) is its counterpart, not its part. If by tasawwur we mean the general sense (knowledge), then tasdiq can be a part of that general category. So there is no part-counterpart contradiction.
The commentator also shows that al-Razi's definition of tasdiq as a compound avoids the issue altogether.

وذلك لأن التصديق إن كان عبارة عن التصور مع الحكم، والتصوّر مع الحكم قسم من التصوّر، وقد جعل في التقسيم المشهور قسيماً له، فيكون قسم الشيء قسيما له - وهو الأمر الأول. وإن كان عبارة عن الحكم، والحكم قسيم للتصور، وقد جعل في التقسيم قسماً من العلم الذي هو نفس التصور، فيكون قسيم الشيء قسماً منه – وهو الأمر الثاني. وهذا الاعتراض إنما يرد إذا قسم العلم إلى مطلق التصور والتصديق) (۱) هذا بناء على أن التصديق عبارة عن الإدراك المجامع للحكم أو المعروض للحكم، كما يدل عليه ظاهر عبارة صاحب الكشف (*) وأتباعه – كالمصنف وغيره - في تقسيم العلم كما بيناه سابقا وأما إذا أريد بالتصديق ماهو مذهب الإمام - أعني المجموع المركب من التصورات الثلاث والحكم - فلايظهر أن التصديق بهذا المعنى قسم من التصوّر، إذ لا يلزم أن يكون المجموع المركب من شيء وآخر بحيث يصدق عليه ذلك الشيء حتى يكون قسماً منه ومندرجا تحته - الاترى أن مجموع الجدار والسقف لا يكون سقفاً ولا جداراً - بل يحتاج حينئذ إلى أن يتمسك بما ذكره الشارح في التصديق بمعني الحكم فيقال : التصديق بمعنى المجموع المركب قسم للتصوّر ؛ كما أنه بمعنى الحكم قسيم له أيضاً، و قد جعلته في التقسيم قسماً من العلم الذي هو نفس التصوّر فيكون قسيم الشيء قسماً منه (شريف).

كشف الأسرار عن غوامض الأفكار لأفضل الدين ناماور الخنجي مخطوط. ٢) من قسم العلم إلى مطلق التصوّر والتصديق لم يرد بالتصور معنى عاماً شاملاً للتصديق، بل أراد بالتصديق إدراك أن النسبة واقعة أوليست بواقعة وأراد بالتصور إدراك ماعدا ذلك، ولاشك أن هذين القسمين متقابلان، ليس أحدهما متناولاً للآخر أصلاً حتى يلزم أن يكون قسم الشيء قسيما له وقسيم الشيء قسماً منه ؛ وأما التصور بمعنى الإدراك مطلقاً - أعني ماهو مرادف للعلم - فهو معنى آخر، ولفظ «التصوّر » يطلق بالاشتراك اللفظي على هذا المعنى - أعني الإدراك مطلقاً - وعلى المعنى الأول - أعني الإدراك المغاير للإدراك المسمّى بالحكم - فلايلزم شيء من المحذورين. أو أراد بالتصديق المجموع المركب من الإدراك والحكم، وأراد بالتصور إدراك ماعدا ذلك، فلا محذور أيضاً، لأن التصديق قسيم للتصور بالمعنى الأخص وقسم من التصوّر بالمعنى الأعم، فلا إشكال على ماهو مراد القوم أصلاً؛ نعم، ظاهر عبارتهم يوهم التباسا يزول بتفسيرهم التصديق والتصور المقابل له - كما قررناه (شریف). (۱) هذا الكلام يدل على أن الاعتراض متوجه على تقسيم المصنف أيضاً، لكنه مندفع بالجواب الذي قرّره الشارح. وأما على التقسيم المشهور : فهو وارد عليه، غير مندفع عنه. وقد عرفت اندفاعه عنه أيضاً بما قررناه، إلا أن اندفاعه أيضًا بما قررناه، إلا أن اندفاعه عن تقسيم المصنف أظهر من اندفاعه عن التقسيم المشهور - كما لا يخفى (شريف).
And that is because if tasdiq is an expression for tasawwur together with hukm, and tasawwur together with hukm is a part of tasawwur, and yet it (tasdiq) has been made in the famous division a counterpart of it (tasawwur), then the part of a thing would be its counterpart—that is the first problem. And if it (tasdiq) is an expression for hukm, while hukm is a counterpart of tasawwur, yet it (tasdiq) has been made in the division a part of knowledge which is itself tasawwur, then the counterpart of a thing would be a part of it—that is the second problem. But this objection only applies if knowledge is divided into absolute tasawwur and tasdiq. (1) This is based on the view that tasdiq is an expression for perception combined with judgment or that which is subject to judgment, as indicated by the apparent wording of the author of al-Kashf and his followers—such as the author (of the text) and others—in their division of knowledge as we previously explained. However, if what is meant by tasdiq is the Imam's position—namely the compound of the three perceptions and judgment—then it is not apparent that tasdiq in this sense is a part of tasawwur, because it is not necessary that a compound of something and another thing be such that the first thing applies to it so that it becomes a part of it and subsumed under it. Do you not see that the compound of wall and ceiling is neither a ceiling nor a wall? Rather, in that case one must resort to what the commentator (al-Sharif) mentioned regarding tasdiq in the sense of hukm, and it is said: tasdiq in the sense of the compound is a part of tasawwur, just as it is also a counterpart of it in the sense of hukm, and it has been made in the division a part of knowledge which is itself tasawwur, so the counterpart of a thing would be a part of it (al-Sharif).

Kashf al-Asrar 'an Ghawamid al-Afkar by Afdal al-Din Namawar al-Khunji (manuscript). 2) Those who divide knowledge into absolute tasawwur and tasdiq do not intend by tasawwur a general meaning including tasdiq; rather, by tasdiq they intend the perception that the relation exists or does not exist, and by tasawwur they intend perception of other than that. There is no doubt that these two divisions are mutually exclusive, neither encompassing the other at all, so it does not follow that a part of a thing is its counterpart or that a counterpart is a part of it. As for tasawwur in the sense of absolute perception—that which is synonymous with knowledge—that is another meaning. The word 'tasawwur' is used homonymously for this meaning—absolute perception—and for the first meaning—perception other than the perception called hukm. Thus, neither of the two problematic consequences arises. Or, if one intends by tasdiq the compound of perception and judgment, and by tasawwur perception of other than that, then there is also no problem, because tasdiq is a counterpart of tasawwur in the specific sense and a part of tasawwur in the general sense. So there is no difficulty regarding what the people (the logicians) intend at all. Yes, the apparent wording of their statements suggests confusion that is removed by their interpretation of tasdiq and the tasawwur opposed to it—as we have established (al-Sharif). (1) This statement indicates that the objection is directed also at the author's division, but it is repelled by the answer that the commentator (al-Sharif) articulated. As for the famous division, the objection applies to it and is not repelled from it. And you have already known that it is repelled from it as well by what we have established, except that its repulsion from the author's division is more apparent than its repulsion from the famous division—as is not hidden (al-Sharif).
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of an objection concerning the division of knowledge (al-`ilm) into tasawwur (conception) and tasdiq (assent). The objection runs that if tasdiq is defined as tasawwur plus judgment (hukm), then it is a part of tasawwur, yet it is made its counterpart in the division (first problem). If tasdiq is defined as the judgment alone, then it is a counterpart of tasawwur, yet it is made a part of knowledge (which is identified with tasawwur) (second problem). The commentator (al-Sharif) shows that this objection only holds against a particular understanding of the division. If one adopts the position of the 'Imam' (Fakhr al-Din al-Razi) that tasdiq is a compound of three perceptions and judgment, then it is not automatically a part of tasawwur because a compound is not simply its component—like a wall-and-ceiling is neither a wall nor a ceiling. Alternatively, if one understands tasawwur in a broader sense (synonymous with knowledge), then tasdiq can be a part of that general tasawwur while still being a counterpart of the specific tasawwur (opposed to judgment). Thus, the apparent inconsistency is resolved by carefully distinguishing the intended meanings of tasawwur and tasdiq. The passage concludes by noting that the objection is more easily repelled from the author's (Qutbi's) division than from the famous division.

Key Terms
تصديق
تصور
حكم
اشتراك لفظي

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does the 'famous division' of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq avoid the objection that tasdiq would be both a part and a counterpart of tasawwur?
A) By defining tasdiq as a compound of perceptions and judgment, so it is not a part of tasawwur.
B) By using tasawwur in the sense of absolute perception (synonymous with knowledge), while tasdiq is defined as perception of a relation.
C) By rejecting the division altogether.
D) By claiming the objection does not apply to the famous division.

Key Takeaway
The objection to the division of knowledge is resolved by recognizing the homonymy of 'tasawwur' and the flexibility in defining 'tasdiq'.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
intermediate
10 min
Resolving Objections by Distinguishing Homonymous Terms: The Case of Tasawwur and Tasdiq
Commentator resolves the objection that tasdiq would be a kind of tasawwur by distinguishing two meanings of 'tasawwur'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a term is used homonymously in a logical definition and explain how that resolves a division objection.

Core Idea
The objection dissolves because 'tasawwur' has two meanings: absolute apprehension and bare conception.

This passage tackles a common logical pitfall: if tasdiq (affirmation) is defined as 'tasawwur with judgment', doesn't that make it a kind of tasawwur, thus invalidating the division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq? The resolution lies in recognizing that 'tasawwur' is homonymous—it can mean either absolute conception (including judgment) or bare conception (without judgment). Understanding this distinction is essential for precise definitions in Islamic logic and jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objection states: if tasdiq = tasawwur + hukm, then tasdiq is a subdivision of tasawwur, so the division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq is invalid (a thing divided into itself and another).
2
Locate the two meanings of 'tasawwur'
The commentator explains that 'tasawwur' can mean (1) absolute mental apprehension (synonymous with knowledge) or (2) bare conception (without judgment). These are homonymous uses.
This is al-ishtirak al-lafdhi (homonymy).
3
Apply the correct meaning to the objection
If 'tasawwur' in the definition means absolute apprehension, then tasdiq is a part of it—no conflict. If it means bare conception, then tasdiq is not a part but rather includes it (since tasdiq = bare conception + judgment). In both cases, the division remains sound.
4
Confirm the resolution via homonymy
The objection only arises if one assumes 'tasawwur' has a single fixed meaning. Once homonymy is acknowledged, both objections are repelled.
This tool is widely used in usul al-fiqh to resolve similar definitional puzzles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما إذا قسم العلم إلى التصور الساذج، وإلى التصديق - كما فعله المصنف - فلا ورود له عليه، لأنا نختار أن التصديق عبارة عن التصوّر مع الحكم، فقوله : «التصوّر مع الحكم قسم من التصور» قلنا : إن أردتم به أنه قسم من التصور الساذج المقابل للتصديق، فظاهر أنه ليس كذلك ؛ وإن أردتم به آنه قسم من مطلق التصوّر فمسلّم، لكن قسيم التصديق ليس مطلق التصوّر، بل التصور الساذج، فلا يلزم أن يكون قسم الشيء قسيماً له. أحدهما متناولاً للآخر أصلاً حتى يلزم أن يكون قسم الشيء قسيما له وقسيم الشيء قسماً منه ؛ وأما التصور بمعنى الإدراك مطلقاً - أعني ماهو مرادف للعلم - فهو معنى آخر، ولفظ «التصوّر » يطلق بالاشتراك اللفظي على هذا المعنى - أعني الإدراك مطلقاً - وعلى المعنى الأول - أعني الإدراك المغاير للإدراك المسمّى بالحكم - فلايلزم شيء من المحذورين. أو أراد بالتصديق المجموع المركب من الإدراك والحكم، وأراد بالتصور إدراك ماعدا ذلك، فلا محذور أيضاً، لأن التصديق قسيم للتصور بالمعنى الأخص وقسم من التصوّر بالمعنى الأعم، فلا إشكال على ماهو مراد القوم أصلاً؛ نعم، ظاهر عبارتهم يوهم التباسا يزول بتفسيرهم التصديق والتصور المقابل له - كما قررناه (شریف). (۱) هذا الكلام يدل على أن الاعتراض متوجه على تقسيم المصنف أيضاً، لكنه مندفع بالجواب الذي قرّره الشارح. وأما على التقسيم المشهور : فهو وارد عليه، غير مندفع عنه. وقد عرفت اندفاعه عنه أيضاً بما قررناه، إلا أن اندفاعه عن تقسيم المصنف أظهر من اندفاعه عن التقسيم المشهور - كما لا يخفى (شريف). الثاني أن المراد بالتصور إما الحضور الذهني مطلقاً أو المقيد بعدم الحكم فإن قلت قوله وجوابه إشارة إلى جواب الاعتراض الثاني إذا أورد على تقسيم المصنف فحاصل كلامه على قياس ما تقدم في الاعتراض الأول أن الاعتراض الثاني أيضاً متوجه على عبارة المصنف إلا أنه مندفع بهذا الجواب وأما على عبارة القوم فهو وارد غير مندفع قلت هذا الجواب كما يدفع الاعتراض الثاني عن كلام المصنف يدفعه عن كلام القوم أيضاً بل هو بكلامهم أنسب لأن كون لفظ التصور مشتركاً بين ما اعتبر فيه عدم الحكم وبين الحضور الذهني مطلقاً إنما يظهر من كلامهم دون كلامه حيث ذكروا التصور في مقابلة التصديق وأرادوا به معنى يقابله قطعا مع أنهم يطلقون التصور على ماكان مرادفاً للعلم أعني الإدراك مطلقاً فللتصور عندهم معنيان وأما كلام المصنف فلا يقتضي إلا أن يكون للتصور معنى واحد متناول للتصور فقط وللتصور مع الحكم وأما أن التصور يطلق على ما يقابل التصديق أعني ما اعتبر فيه عدم الحكم فلا دلالة عليه أصلاً لأنه جعل التصور فقط مقابلاً للتصديق فاعتبار عدم الحكم مستفاد من قيد فقط وليس داخلاً في مفهوم لفظ التصور بل هو مستعمل بمعنى الإدراك مطلقاً وقد ضم إليه قيداً زائداً و جعل المقيد قسيماً للتصديق فللتصور عنده معنى واحد فاتضح بما ذكرناه أن الاشتراك في لفظ التصور إنما يظهر من كلامهم دون كلامه وبهذا الاشتراك يندفع الاعتراضان معاً على التقسيم المشهور وأما اندفاعهما عن تقسيم المصنف فإنما هو الجواب الأول لأن المقابل
As for if he divides knowledge into bare conception and affirmation — as the author did — then no objection applies to it, because we choose that affirmation is conception with judgment. So his statement: 'conception with judgment is a division of conception' — we say: if you mean by it that it is a division of bare conception which is the opposite of affirmation, then it is clear that it is not so; and if you mean by it that it is a division of absolute conception, then it is granted, but the co-ordinate of affirmation is not absolute conception but bare conception, so it does not follow that a division of a thing is its co-ordinate. One of them does not encompass the other at all such that a division of a thing would be its co-ordinate and a co-ordinate of a thing would be a division of it. As for conception in the meaning of absolute apprehension — i.e., what is synonymous with knowledge — it is another meaning, and the word 'conception' is applied by homonymy to this meaning — i.e., absolute apprehension — and to the first meaning — i.e., the apprehension other than the apprehension called judgment — so none of the two problems arise. Or if he meant by affirmation the composite whole composed of apprehension and judgment, and by conception the apprehension of what is other than that, then there is also no problem, because affirmation is a co-ordinate of conception in the specific sense and a division of conception in the general sense, so there is no difficulty in what the people intend at all; yes, the apparent meaning of their expression gives rise to confusion that is removed by their interpretation of affirmation and the conception opposite to it — as we have established (Sharif). (1) This statement indicates that the objection applies to the author's division as well, but it is repelled by the answer that the commentator presented. As for the famous division, it applies to it and is not repelled from it. And you have known that it is repelled from it as well by what we have established, except that its repulsion from the author's division is more apparent than its repulsion from the famous division — as is not hidden (Sharif). Second: that by 'conception' is meant either absolute mental presence or restricted by absence of judgment. For if you say: his statement 'and its answer' refers to the answer to the second objection when it is raised against the author's division, so the summary of his statement — in analogy with what preceded in the first objection — is that the second objection also applies to the author's expression, except that it is repelled by this answer; and as for the people's expression, it applies and is not repelled. I say: this answer repels the second objection from the author's statement just as it repels it from the people's statement; rather, it is more suitable to their statement, because the fact that the word 'conception' is shared between what considers the absence of judgment and absolute mental presence only appears from their statement, not from his statement, since they mentioned conception in opposition to affirmation and intended by it a meaning that definitely opposes it, while they also apply conception to what is synonymous with knowledge — i.e., absolute apprehension — so for them conception has two meanings. As for the author's statement, it only requires that conception has one meaning encompassing 'conception only' and 'conception with judgment'; and that conception is applied to what is opposite to affirmation — i.e., what considers the absence of judgment — there is no indication of that at all, because he made 'conception only' the opposite of affirmation, so the consideration of absence of judgment is derived from the qualifier 'only' and is not included in the concept of the word 'conception'. Rather, it is used in the meaning of absolute apprehension, and he added an extra qualifier and made the qualified the co-ordinate of affirmation, so for him conception has one meaning. It has become clear from what we have mentioned that the homonymy in the word 'conception' only appears from their statement, not from his, and by this homonymy both objections are repelled from the famous division. As for their repulsion from the author's division, it is only by the first answer, because the opposite
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary addressing an objection raised against the division of knowledge into tasawwur (conception) and tasdiq (affirmation). The objection goes: if tasdiq is defined as 'tasawwur with judgment', then it would be a kind of tasawwur, making the division one of a thing into itself and its other — a logical flaw. The commentator resolves this by distinguishing two meanings of 'tasawwur'. First, tasawwur can mean bare conception (without judgment), which is the opposite of tasdiq. Second, tasawwur can mean absolute apprehension (including judgment), which is broader. When tasdiq is said to be 'tasawwur with judgment', if 'tasawwur' here means absolute apprehension, then tasdiq is a part of it, and the division is fine because tasdiq is a co-ordinate of the specific tasawwur (bare) but a part of the general tasawwur (absolute). Alternatively, if 'tasawwur' in the definition means bare conception, then tasdiq is not a part of it but includes it, so again no problem. The commentator then notes that the ambiguity (ishtirak lafdhi) in the word 'tasawwur' is what resolves the objection. The commentary by Sharif (al-Jurjani) adds that this resolution works for both the author's division and the famous division, but it is more apparent for the author's. The passage then discusses a second point: that 'tasawwur' can mean either absolute mental presence or restricted by absence of judgment. The response clarifies that the homonymy (sharing of a word between two meanings) is evident in the statements of the earlier scholars (the 'people'), but not in the author's, because the author uses 'tasawwur' in one sense (absolute apprehension) and adds 'only' to restrict it. Thus, the objection is repelled in both cases, but by different answers.

Key Terms
التصوّر (al-tasawwur)
التصديق (al-tasdiq)
الاشتراك اللفظي (al-ishtirak al-lafdhi)

Checkpoint
How does the commentator resolve the objection that tasdiq would be a kind of tasawwur, making the division invalid?
A) By denying that tasdiq includes any element of conception.
B) By pointing out that 'tasawwur' is used homonymously for absolute conception and bare conception.
C) By redefining tasdiq as something entirely separate from tasawwur.
D) By claiming the objection does not apply to the author's division.

Key Takeaway
Recognizing homonymy (al-ishtirak al-lafdhi) in key terms resolves apparent contradictions in logical divisions.

Identify an instance of homonymy in the definition of 'salah' (prayer) in fiqh: sometimes it means any supplication, sometimes the specific ritual. Explain how clarifying these two meanings resolves a potential objection about the validity of a non-ritual supplication.

In the passage, the commentator says 'tasawwur' is used by homonymy. Find another example from Islamic logic or usul where a term like 'dalil' (evidence) or 'amr' (command) is homonymous, and show how the same resolution technique would apply.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
advanced
10 min
Resolving Objections Through the Ambiguity of 'Tasawwur'
Commentator resolves an objection about the two meanings of 'tasawwur'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two meanings of 'tasawwur' and explain how their ambiguity resolves the logical objections to the division of knowledge into conception and assent.

Core Idea
Tasawwur is ambiguous: it can mean bare conception or absolute mental presence, and this ambiguity prevents logical contradictions.

In Islamic logic, the division of knowledge into tasawwur (conception) and tasdiq (assent) faced two objections: (1) if tasawwur means absolute mental presence, the division is self-division; (2) if it means bare conception, it cannot be a component of tasdiq. The commentator Sharif al-Jurjani shows that the term 'tasawwur' is ambiguous, and distinguishing its two meanings resolves both objections cleanly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections
Read the passage and locate where the two objections are stated. The first objection is about self-division (tasawwur as absolute mental presence = knowledge itself). The second is about the impossibility of tasawwur being part of tasdiq if it excludes judgment.
2
Extract the two meanings of 'tasawwur'
From the resolution, note that 'tasawwur' has two meanings: (1) bare conception, which is mental presence conditioned by absence of judgment (bi-shart la shay); (2) absolute mental presence, which is unconditioned (la bi-shart shay) and synonymous with knowledge. The passage uses the threefold conditioning framework: bi-shart shay (with judgment = tasdiq), bi-shart la shay (without judgment = bare tasawwur), la bi-shart shay (absolute = the genus).
3
Apply the first meaning to the division
In the division of knowledge, tasawwur (as a species) is bare conception, which contrasts with tasdiq (assent). So the division is into two distinct types: bare conception vs. judgment-involving conception.
4
Apply the second meaning to the composition
When tasdiq is said to require tasawwur, it means absolute mental presence—the genus that includes both bare conception and judgment. So tasdiq contains tasawwur in the absolute sense, not the bare sense.
5
Verify both objections are resolved
The first objection is resolved because the division is not self-division: it divides knowledge into two species under the genus. The second is resolved because the tasawwur included in tasdiq is the absolute sense, not the bare sense, so no contradiction.

لأنّ «الحضور الذهني مطلقاً» نفس العلم - وإن عني به المقيد بعدم الحكم، امتنع اعتبار التصوّر في التصديق، لأن عدم الحكم حينئذ يكون معتبراً في التصوّر ، فلو كان التصور معتبراً في التصديق لكان عدم الحكم معتبراً فيه - والحكم معتبرفيه أيضاً - فيلزم اعتبار الحكم وعدمه في التصديق، وإنه محال وجوابه : أن التصوّر يطلق بالاشتراك على ما اعتبر فيه عدم الحكم - وهو التصوّر الساذج - وعلى الحضور الذهني مطلقاً - كما وقع التنبيه عليه - والمعتبر في التصديق ليس هو الأول، بل الثاني. - والحاصل أن الحضور الذهني مطلقاً هو العلم، والتصوّر إما أن يعتبر بشرط شيء» - أي الحكم - ويقال له التصديق، أو «بشرط لاشيء» - أي عدم الحكم - ويقال له التصوّر الساذج، أو «لا بشرط شيء» وهو مطلق التصور ؛ فالمقابل للتصديق هو «التصوّر بشرط لاشيء»، والمعتبر للتصديق عنده كما صرح به هو التصور فقط، وليس التصديق قسماً منه، بل هو قسم من التصوّر مطلقاً، فاندفع الاعتراض الأول، فلا يلزم أن يكون قسم الشيء قسيماً له. وكذا المعتبر في التصديق - If you say: His statement 'And its answer' refers to the answer to the second objection when raised against the author's division. The gist of his words—analogous to what preceded in the first objection—is that the second objection also applies to the author's expression, except that it is repelled by this answer. As for the expression of the [other] scholars, it is problematic and not repelled. I say: This answer, just as it repels the second objection from the author's words, also repels it from the scholars' words; rather, it is more suitable to their words. Because the fact that the expression 'tasawwur' is ambiguous (mushtarak) between [that] in which absence of judgment is considered and between absolute mental presence appears only from their words, not from his words. For they mentioned tasawwur in contrast to tasdiq and meant by it a meaning that definitely contrasts it; nevertheless they also use tasawwur as synonymous with knowledge—meaning absolute apprehension. Thus tasawwur has two meanings for them. As for the author's words, they only require that tasawwur have a single meaning covering 'tasawwur only' and 'tasawwur with judgment'. As for tasawwur being used for what contrasts tasdiq—meaning that in which absence of judgment is considered—there is no indication of that at all. Because he made 'tasawwur only' a counterpart of tasdiq, so the consideration of absence of judgment is derived from the qualifier 'only' and is not included in the concept of the word 'tasawwur'. Rather, it is used in the sense of absolute apprehension, and a qualifier is attached to it, and the qualified is made a counterpart of tasdiq. Thus tasawwur has a single meaning for him. So it is clear from what we have mentioned that the ambiguity in the word tasawwur appears only from their words, not from his words. And by this ambiguity both objections are repelled against the well-known division. As for their being repelled from the author's division, that is only through the first answer, because the counterpart of judgment, if by it is meant absolute mental presence, then the division of a thing into itself and another is entailed—since 'absolute mental presence' is knowledge itself. And if by it is meant that which is qualified by absence of judgment, then considering tasawwur in tasdiq becomes impossible, because absence of judgment would then be considered in tasawwur. So if tasawwur were considered in tasdiq, then absence of judgment would be considered in it—while judgment is also considered in it—thus requiring the consideration of judgment and its absence in tasdiq, which is impossible. And its answer: Tasawwur is used ambiguously for that in which absence of judgment is considered—which is bare tasawwur—and for absolute mental presence—as has been noted. The one considered in tasdiq is not the first, but the second. The summary: Absolute mental presence is knowledge, and tasawwur is either considered 'conditioned by something'—i.e., judgment—called tasdiq, or 'conditioned by nothing'—i.e., absence of judgment—called bare tasawwur, or 'unconditioned'—which is absolute tasawwur. So the counterpart of tasdiq is 'tasawwur conditioned by nothing', and what is considered in tasdiq according to him—as he clarified—is absolute tasawwur, not tasawwur only. Tasdiq is not a division of it; rather, it is a division of absolute tasawwur. So the first objection is repelled, and it is not required that a division of a thing be its counterpart. Similarly, what is considered in tasdiq—as condition or part—is absolute tasawwur, not tasawwur only. Absence of judgment is considered only in tasawwur only, not in absolute tasawwur. Thus the second objection is also repelled (Sharif).
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement where the commentator (likely Sharif al-Jurjani) addresses an objection regarding the definition of tasawwur and tasdiq in logic. The objection is that if tasawwur is defined as mere mental presence (al-hudhur al-dhihni mutlaqan), then dividing knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq would be a division of something into itself and another, since mere mental presence is identical to knowledge. If tasawwur is defined as mental presence conditioned by absence of judgment (al-muqayyad bi 'adam al-hukm), then it cannot be a part of tasdiq (which involves judgment), because that would entail a contradiction: both judgment and absence of judgment would be present in tasdiq. The resolution is that the term 'tasawwur' is ambiguous (mushtarak). It has two meanings: (1) bare conception (al-tasawwur al-sadhi) which is mental presence conditioned by absence of judgment, and (2) absolute mental presence (al-hudhur al-dhihni mutlaqan) which includes both tasawwur and tasdiq. The author's division uses 'tasawwur' in the first sense as the counterpart of tasdiq, while 'tasawwur' in the second sense is the genus that includes both. Thus, when tasdiq is said to require tasawwur, it means absolute mental presence, not the bare conception. Therefore, neither objection applies. The commentator then explains that this ambiguity is clearer in the statements of the earlier logicians (al-qawm) than in the author's (al-Muhaqqiq al-Tusi's) words, because the author's expression suggests only one meaning of tasawwur. Nonetheless, the ambiguity resolves the issue in both cases. The passage uses a distinction familiar in Islamic logic: the threefold consideration of 'bi-shart shay'', 'bi-shart la shay'', and 'la bi-shart shay'' (conditioned by something, conditioned by nothing, unconditioned). This classification is applied to tasawwur to show how the same concept can function in different roles without contradiction.

Checkpoint

A) The mere mental image of 'prayer' without affirming or denying any ruling.
B) The judgment that 'prayer is obligatory.'
C) The doubt whether 'prayer is obligatory.'
D) The absolute mental presence of the concept 'prayer,' which is present even in the judgment that it is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The ambiguity of the term 'tasawwur' between bare conception and absolute mental presence allows it to function as both the genus and a species of knowledge without logical contradiction.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
